Iâ€™m a firm believer that what weâ€™re seeing here is the Wolfâ€™s Trial, but as a warrior from Noxus would see it. We know that the way Kindred appears is different for every culture, and often just for any individual in general. Here we see Ambessa facing death after battle, an arrow shot through her, and being offered a different path- a path to life, to all the things she could ever want, while giving up the chance for a quick and easy death, by releasing her lamb. Instead, she chose to fight the Chosen of the Wolf, the remnant figures who have fought Kindred and survived, given another chance- Atreus surviving his experience as the Aspect of War, Swayne surviving his own near-death experience, and the others are left up to question. She ultimately loses the fight, but she displays courage and resilience- traits she would need that honor her choice to survive. And in the end, sheâ€™s given her second chance, and revived, giving life to not only herself- but to her children, to Kino, and later Mel herself. Given that we know she later meets a man during her war march, it can be surmised that the man in question is also potentially either a Solari or an Aspect Host, given Melâ€™s powers.  Ambessa chose to become a conqueror then, to give up a peaceful life in order to give her family everything. Unfortunately, her conquest only cost her everything- her son, her relationship with her daughter, all of her alliances, thousands of her men, and eventually her own life. But in so doing, she set up Mel to take her place, to become the Wolf- the very being who gave her the chance to become something more.

After watching Act 3 of Arcane, I think more and more that Ambessa is going to be the next Pantheon.  First of all, they introduce a new champ to the game only to canonically kill them off a month later? Idk. Seems odd.  Secondly, the Kindred imagery here is STRONG. Kindred is death incarnate, and here we see Ambessa accepting some kind of gift from them. Considering Ambessa died in the final act, and the imagery presented here, with her rising from death... combine that with the fact we see the last Pantheon (Atreus) in this video fighting Ambessa, which may very well be the Aspect testing her to see if she is worthy.  This gift from Kindred could be the renewal of life, a rebirthing. No longer Ambessa, but instead becoming the new Aspect of War itself. We see how she transforms and has her new outfit as soon as she accepts the gift from Kindred, fully stepping into her new role as Aspect, with golden armor and symbols which are very similar to Pantheon's. Ambessa had never used golden before then.  Through countless battles and struggles, her scars become golden, showing how she proves herself in the eyes of the Aspect, who ends up choosing her to become its new vessel on earth and grants her new life.

give Ambessa's VA a MASSIVE pay raise
I think her soul was being judged by death. It seems like the spirit of death before the split into kindred/wolf, as the mask is much different and has a more even blend of both aspects (light/dark or peace/violence). The lyrics themselves are tightly woven into what is happening. Her soul is scarred from her struggles which mainly seem to stem from violence and fighting. She has a goal to lead, represented by the throne she desires so much that she's practically crawling at some point. Her demons are the thoughts and belief she has that the only way to achieve peace, is to be on top no matter what that requires from her.  Injured after a battle, death comes to her. It sees how much will she has to live and it offers her a chance. Her baby's soul, represented as the lamb, is offered up as a sacrifice as she's harassed by her inner demons. Although she seems to try and protect it at first, her dream of ruling overtakes the desire to protect her innocent child. We see the anguish of it, but also the side of her that is determined and full of conviction to keep on fighting/climbing. I believe in a way, this sacrifice hardens her spiritually/mentally/emotionally as it's represented as armor -cold, hard, and unyielding as she keeps moving forward. But then I think the baby is still possibly alive. Energized by some energy, possibly because it inherits Ambessa's strength and character or the wolf sees both worthy to keep on struggling.

I'm fascinated by the depth of discussion within the League of Legends community surrounding the lore of Runeterra. The collective passion and insight of fans bring rich layers of understanding to the complex world-building and narrative that underpin the game. Riot Games would do well to tap into this intellectual fervor, as the comments section is a treasure trove of innovative ideas and thoughtful analysis.

In lore, the kindred (wolf in this case) is only visible to someone dead or dying, and they always kill their target. The fact that Ambessa saw the wolf and it didn't take her life means that the wolf wasn't there for her but instead it was for her child.   The lamb could symbolize the way Ambessa is protecting the child from the spirits of death, keeping it's innocence. Since it's the wolf Ambessa needs to fight to prove her worth, in the end the child still dies, but The Kindred acknowledges their struggle and grants Ambessa some kind of clarity (or some kind of power) symbolized by the Wolfhead Heart given towards the end of the video.   Top notch lore faithfulness and storytelling from these guys, Riot never misses.

(If you are watching this video after the necrit video, this scene should be at minute 23:40 in his video) And she crying to the child holding another sheep, that -  I understud as - his daughter... cause they will die togheter if Ambessa doesn't struggle for her life... Ught. Perfection.  I'm also thrilled that Riot and Fortiche chose to portray death through a cultural lens, incorporating both animated and cultural references. It's fantastic to see how the concept of the 'Reaper' embodied by the sheep and wolf changes to match with religions that don't focus on death as an individual experience. This is why dying as a Shuriman is a communal ritual involving dance, music, a mediator, and the presence of other departed souls.  Noxus, drawing inspiration from Rome, emphasizes anthropocentrism and individualism, reflecting modern values rooted in Greco-Roman culture. However, Ambessa's perspective on death is distinctly different. Even in her solitary battle against the wolf, she draws strength from her ancestors. It's Ambessa's ancestors who give her strength, literally undoing the lamb made to die without fighting in what is what will make her alive.  In religions/cultures of African matrix, death is a collective experience and that's why connecting with the dead can only be done through rituals that involve many people. Ambessa is not only Shuriman, but also she is not Noxian, thats why death is white-golden and dark-red in different moments. It's a very sensitive way of approaching how cultures interact without canceling each other out.  Notice she's already pregnant, her hand resting on her belly instead of the arrow. As she 'gains life', her daughter also awakens. It's intriguing that Ambessa turns her scars into gold post-battle, yet they don't manifest physically. Could the magic of facing death and returning have altered Mel, causing her scars to become corporeal?  Arcane has a remarkable ability to elevate everything it touches.
